Inserting <br> within a paragraph to enforce line break for poetry or addresses

Using <hr> between sections of an article to signal a visual and logical pause ^YYjEboz7

<br>: Empty element, no attributes required, optional clear attribute (obsolete in HTML5)

<hr>: Empty element, may include attributes like width, size, and align (deprecated in HTML5) ^AAEjCni6

Using <br> to create vertical spacing instead of CSS margin or padding

Misusing <hr> for layout purposes instead of semantic division

Writing <br></br> or <hr></hr>, despite both being void elements ^N6TyCtoo

<br> vs <p>: <br> breaks lines within content, whereas <p> separates paragraphs as block elements.

<hr> vs CSS borders: <hr> adds a semantic divider, while borders are strictly stylistic. ^Bztg3oft

The <br> and <hr> HTML elements serve as semantic and structural tools for controlling content layout without introducing new block elements. <br> (line break) inserts an explicit line break within inline content, forcing the browser to render the following content on a new line without creating a new block. It is an empty element and must not contain content. <hr> (horizontal rule) generates a thematic break represented visually as a horizontal line, signaling a division between sections of content. It is also an empty element and is often used to separate thematic shifts within a document, though it carries no semantic meaning beyond visual demarcation in most user agents. ^U3NVni90
